Soft shell crab roll on postmates is $6.25, but walk into the store and it's $8.95
The same occurred on EVERY item in my order.

< review>
I Strickly come for the bargain priced(daily
Specials)Combination plates not the Sushi Rolls. Their Daily Specials are offered for both Lunch and Dinner which is rare because most Japanese places only offer Specials for Lunch. I usually get the #1 Special which is usually Teriyaki, Ginger, or Garlic Chicken and is served with Fried Gyoza(4 pcs.) White Rice, and Miso Soup along with Salad.>> and then add 2 egg rolls. It's very reasonably priced compared to most other Japanese places and the quality is good. If you want Nobu this isn't the place but if you want a tasty, casual, quick, inexpensive decent quality place Ichiban in PB is a great option.<//review>

<Text>I have been coming to Ichiban for at least 15 years, probably longer. I should have written this review a long time ago.

Basically, this place serves affordable, decent sushi. They have an affordable happy hour as well. You order first, and sometimes it can take a while to order when it is busy. But this means there is almost always seating once the order is done. You can also call in your order for takeout. The important thing, is you can get a sushi roll (look at the special menu) for the price of a good burrito. For their other hot food, eat it before it gets cold.
My personal favorite rolls are the Orange Blossom roll, and their Caterpillar roll.
The staff are also very friendly and helpful.</Text><Pics>None</Pics><Resp>None</Resp><Gmap_id>0x80dc01c01b003867:0x89d3af061f3f2bea< /Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

<gmapID>0x80dc01c01b003867:0x89d3af061f3f2bea<//gmapID><username>Karen Orell</username>< text>
This is a real find if you love sushi and also sushi at a great price.  Special rolls are 10 pieces rather than the 6 or 8 typically found at sushi bars. And the pricing is well below what I generally pay at competitors- actually about half.  The staff is attentive and the sushi very tasty.  There is also another location in Claremont at the 805 and Claremont Mesa Blvd which I've eaten at as well.  Not fancy but you can get a great deal at either location.</text>

<pictures>None</pictures><text>I messed up the order, guys accepted replacement with no questions. Grate service, friendly staff, taste good as well.</text><Gmap_id>0x80dc01c01b003867:0x89d3af061f3f2bea<//Gmap_id><name>sam smith<//name><Resp>None< /Resp>< time>

102133424225038773126<//user>

<rating>2<//rating><response>None</response>< userid>
110490848155879882552<//userid>
< text>
I see that a lot of people like this place. To each their own, I suppose.

The ordering system is not efficient and very inconvenient. They expect you to look at a posted menu and remember what you want when you get to the counter. For a guy like me, it's difficult to remember the 5 rolls I want. Especially when there's a line out the door behind you. Which leads me to the next issue, in that there are no descriptions of the rolls anywhere. So what's in a chefs roll? Or the Baja roll? So they told me to take a sushi check list to the table with me and my server would come get it. They never picked it up so  we took it up front ourselves. Well as I'm still making my selections, my girlfriend's chicken teriyaki arrived at the table. Needless to say that my girlfriend had to sit there and wait for me to finish eating. One of the worst things a restaurant can do is not time their food correctly (I'm a chef, I know). I eat a lot of sushi and as much as I hate to say it, it will not be here.

The only reason I'm giving it 2 stars is because the cooks did good work. But they can't carry the restaurant with a terrible FOH operation.</text>

Been going there for many years. Hasn't killed me yet. Here's the thing about Ichiban PB: the food will never delight you, but never disappoint you. Sometimes the service is very good and personal, sometimes ambivalent at best. The food quality NEVER varies; it's like it's popped out of the sushi machine. The bronze-standard for San Diego sushi. (Can I get some extra wasabi, please?) Be sure to check the glass display case up front for the discounted specials. And if you're a newby: Order FIRST, then sit. <text>Went here a few years ago, when I had some business at the "San Antonio Winery".... "Lanza Bros. Market  & Delicatessen" is the real article,serving a large variety of great sandwiches,wines, cold beer  and deli specialties...They have chairs and tables out front, so you  can watch the cars go by,while eating your sandwich.... or take your order to go....This place has an urban "old school" L.A./NY vibe to the place...with the deli case and all...it seems like it's been there for years,and it has... Est.1927....not just your run -of- the- mill variety store,even though they carry everything your typical variety store would carry...not fancy,but down to earth...This is where the locals "do lunch"....I had the chicken salad, the tuna salad, or the roast beef,I can't  remember which...All I remember is, it was delicious...When visiting Downtown L.A., stop by Lanza Bros.Market & Deli...Enjoy!
FYI:
‚òÜThey don't accept credit cards,but F.Y.C., they do have an ATM in the store...

‚òÜThey don't sell fresh bulk produce,accept the veggies served  in the salads and sandwiches....They serve hot soups, featuring homemade Minestrone soup...They serve a Green Salad, with your choice of meats served on it, or topped with chicken salad or tuna salad.... "cold cuts"(deli meats) and cheeses sold and cut to order, priced by the pound~<//text><date>1483893049041<//date><pics>None<//pics><UserId.>105285796148081525717< /UserId.><Rate>4</Rate></record>

Now I have brought my husband over in the past year and we have loved  getting to know Dr. Agrawal and Laura.

They are so quick, and we got our cleanings done and out the door. They checked our temperature, required masks upon arrival, they were wearing masks the entire time,  had a hand washing station ready, and friendly sign to welcome us in!

<review>We decided to get breakfast there because we saw some reviews online and we also read some that stated that they just got remodeled on restaurants impossible. We like that show so we were pretty excited to go there and check it out. Things started out pretty well it was obvious that it was professionally remodeled, and it looked great. When we ordered things started to go downhill. We both ordered breakfast and we are told that they're out of hashbrowns so we had a get tater tots instead. They want to breakfast team one of them actually had hashbrowns and we got them to get us more hashbrowns for the other plate. One dish we ordered was the veggie omelette which was actually pretty good, however the hashbrowns were pretty bland. The other dish we ordered was a breakfast with potatoes eggs and biscuits and gravy, which we're told there out of biscuits then the guy tried to get us to get toast with gravy. Are you serious toast with gravy come on? I ended up getting French toast instead which was pretty bland my eggs were supposed to be over easy they came out more like over medium. While we sat and ate our breakfast we could tell that there were other tables I had issues with their food. Overall we are not really that impressed and don't think will be back for a long time. Chef Robert Irvine along with restaurants impossible was only there two weeks ago and I think someone needs to let him know that he needs to go back and fix this place. The episode is going to air in March 2014, and I hope they get their act together by then or else they're not gonna be able to watch their own show.< /review>< Rating>
